  1378. # [11:36] <AryehGregor> fox2mike, you won't corrupt it. OPTIMIZE on InnoDB is the same as ALTER, which works by locking the table, making a copy, and then atomically overwriting the original table with the copy. If you kill it, it will just delete the copy and unlock the original.
  1379. # [11:36] * Joins: twi (Adium@moz-87047FBA.cust.dsl.vodafone.it)
  1380. # [11:37] <AryehGregor> Well, master <-> master is pretty much the same as master -> slave, because you make sure that one of the masters is always read-only. Otherwise you have data corruption. master <-> master really just means master -> slave but you can easily switch the master, it's kind of a MySQL implementation detail.
  1381. # [11:37] <AryehGregor> (they're both reading each others' replogs, which is why it's called master-master, but only one of them had better be writing its own statements to the replog at once, or else Bad Stuff Will Happen)
